hamiltonian circuit aysend theoeyy Wait train mein baslyavar pathavto Module 5: Algebraic Structures

Algebraic Structures with One Binary Operation

1. Semigroup: A set with a single binary operation that is closed and associative. It means if you take any two elements from the set, their operation result is also in the set, and the order of grouping operations doesn't affect the outcome.


2. Monoid: A semigroup with an identity element. This means there’s an element in the set that, when combined with any other element using the binary operation, leaves that element unchanged.


3. Group: A monoid where every element has an inverse. In other words, for every element in the group, there is another element in the set such that combining them using the group operation yields the identity element.


4. Subgroup: A subset of a group that itself satisfies the group properties. That is, it must be closed under the group operation, contain the identity element, and have inverses for each element in the subset.


5. Abelian Group: A group where the operation is commutative, meaning the order in which you combine two elements doesn’t affect the result. All elements of the group "commute" with each other.


6. Cyclic Group: A group generated by a single element, meaning every element in the group can be obtained by repeatedly applying the group operation to this generator element.


7. Isomorphism: A structure-preserving mapping between two algebraic structures (like groups or rings) that shows a one-to-one correspondence between elements of the structures and preserves the operation.



Algebraic Structures with Two Binary Operations

1. Ring: A set equipped with two binary operations (typically addition and multiplication) satisfying certain properties, such as being an Abelian group under addition and a semigroup under multiplication. Rings are foundational in abstract algebra and are used to generalize arithmetic operations.



Coding Theory

1. Coding: The process of converting data into a form suitable for transmission or storage. Codes are structured in a way that helps detect and correct errors.


2. Binary Information and Error Detection: Information in coding theory is often represented in binary (0s and 1s). Error detection techniques identify errors in binary data, often through the use of redundant bits or checksums.


3. Decoding: The process of converting coded data back into its original form. Decoding involves translating binary sequences into understandable information.


4. Error Correction: Techniques used to correct errors in data transmission or storage. Common methods include Hamming codes and Reed-Solomon codes, which can detect and correct errors by analyzing the code structure.




---

Module 6: Graph Theory

1. Types of Graphs: Various kinds of graphs, such as simple graphs, multigraphs, and weighted graphs. Each type has unique properties depending on the edges and vertices.


2. Graph Representation: Methods for representing a graph, such as adjacency lists, adjacency matrices, and incidence matrices.


3. Subgraphs: A subset of a graph’s vertices and edges that forms a graph itself. A subgraph contains a portion of the original graph.


4. Operations on Graphs: Actions performed on graphs, like union, intersection, and product, which combine or modify existing graphs in specific ways.


5. Walk, Path, Circuit:

Walk: A sequence of vertices where each consecutive pair is connected by an edge.

Path: A walk with no repeated vertices, representing a way to go from one vertex to another.

Circuit: A path that starts and ends at the same vertex.



6. Connected Graphs: A graph where there’s a path between every pair of vertices, ensuring there are no isolated parts.


7. Disconnected Graph: A graph with multiple parts or "components" that are not connected by paths.


8. Components: Distinct subgraphs of a disconnected graph that are themselves connected.


9. Homomorphism and Isomorphism of Graphs:

Homomorphism: A mapping from one graph to another that preserves adjacency.

Isomorphism: A bijective mapping between two graphs that preserves structure, meaning the graphs are structurally identical.



10. Euler and Hamiltonian Graphs:

Eulerian Graph: A graph containing an Euler circuit, which is a circuit that visits every edge exactly once.

Hamiltonian Graph: A graph containing a Hamiltonian circuit, which is a circuit that visits every vertex exactly once.



11. Planar Graph: A graph that can be drawn on a plane without any edges crossing each other.


12. Cut Set: A set of edges whose removal increases the number of connected components, effectively breaking connections within the graph.


13. Cut Vertex: A vertex that, when removed along with its incident edges, increases the number of connected components.


14. Applications: Graph theory has numerous applications in areas like networking, biology, computer science (e.g., algorithms for shortest paths, network reliability), and social science for modeling relationships. aaj ghe na mentos polo🤭 Ghetla lobby madhe thambtoy? same class nasnar na Haa 11th var jauya tu alyavar bhai mi ale ki ekda What's ur eta ? ashi oral revision karuya pls ??? Slide 1: Introduction
Presenter: Good [morning/afternoon/evening] everyone,
Today, I’m here to introduce an innovative solution that simplifies the complex process of assigning invigilation duties. Our Invigilation Duty Allocation System is a web application designed to make duty assignments effortless for administrators while providing teachers with a seamless way to access their schedules and remuneration details.


---

Slide 2: The Problem
Assigning invigilation duties has always been a challenging task. Why?

For Admins: They manually create duty rosters, balance workloads, and allocate blocks, often leading to scheduling conflicts and inefficiencies.

For Teachers: It’s difficult to track assigned duties, changes in timetables, and remuneration calculations.

For Institutions: Errors in duty allocation can lead to staffing issues during exams, causing stress and confusion.


A more organized, automated, and transparent solution is necessary.


---

Slide 3: The Solution – Our Web Application
Our Invigilation Duty Allocation System automates the entire process, ensuring smooth operations for both admins and teachers. The system provides:

Automated Scheduling: Assigns duties based on workload, availability, and predefined rules.

Timetable Generation: Creates structured, error-free exam schedules in minutes.

Block Allocation: Ensures every exam hall has designated invigilators.

Remuneration Calculation: Tracks invigilation payments accurately.

Teacher Dashboard: Allows teachers to view their duties, schedules, and earnings in real time.


This system eliminates manual effort, scheduling conflicts, and miscommunication.


---

Slide 4: How It Works (Admin Panel)

1. Create an Exam Session: Admins input the exam schedule and duration.


2. Enter Teacher Details: Availability, workload, and preferences are recorded.


3. Automate Duty Allocation: The system ensures fair and balanced distribution.


4. Generate Timetables & Block Assignments: Printable and digital schedules are created.


5. Remuneration Calculation: Automatic computation of payments for each teacher.



With this system, administrators save hours of effort and reduce errors.


---

Slide 5: How It Works (Teacher Panel)

1. Login & Dashboard Access: Teachers securely log in to view their assigned duties.


2. Check Duty Charts: Clearly structured duty schedules at their fingertips.


3. View Total Remuneration: Real-time tracking of their earnings.


4. Notifications & Updates: Instant alerts for any schedule changes or additional assignments.



No more last-minute confusion or miscommunication.


---

Slide 6: Key Benefits
✔ For Admins: Drastically reduces workload, minimizes scheduling conflicts, and ensures fair duty allocation.
✔ For Teachers: Provides instant access to duty schedules and payment details, reducing stress.
✔ For Institutions: Creates a smooth and transparent examination process, improving overall efficiency.

The system is designed to make invigilation duty simpler, faster, and more reliable for everyone involved.


---

Slide 7: Live Demo / Prototype (if applicable)
[Showcase a quick walkthrough of the application’s features, highlighting how effortlessly admins can assign duties and how easily teachers can access their schedules.]


---

Slide 8: Conclusion & Call to Action
With the Invigilation Duty Allocation System, we eliminate the stress and errors associated with traditional scheduling methods. Our system ensures efficiency, accuracy, and transparency, making it a must-have for educational institutions.

Thank you for your time! I’d be happy to answer any questions.


---

This version keeps everything clear, professional, and a little more detailed without overcomplicating things. Slide 1: Introduction
Good [morning/afternoon/evening] everyone,
Assigning invigilation duties is often time-consuming and complicated. Our Invigilation Duty Allocation System automates the process, making it efficient for admins and easily accessible for teachers.


---

Slide 2: The Problem

Admins struggle with manual scheduling, workload balancing, and block allocation.

Teachers face confusion about duty assignments and last-minute changes.

Institutions experience inefficiencies and scheduling conflicts.


A smarter, automated solution is needed.


---

Slide 3: The Solution
Our web application simplifies the process with:
✔ Automated Scheduling – Assigns duties fairly based on availability.
✔ Timetable Generation – Creates structured exam schedules.
✔ Block Allocation – Ensures every exam hall has invigilators.
✔ Teacher Dashboard – Provides real-time access to duty details.

No more manual errors or miscommunication!


---

Slide 4: How It Works (Admin Panel)

1. Set Exam Session & Teacher Availability


2. Automate Duty Allocation & Generate Timetables


3. Assign Blocks & Publish Duty Charts


4. Send Notifications for Any Changes



Saves time, ensures fairness, and reduces workload!


---

Slide 5: How It Works (Teacher Panel)

1. Login to Dashboard – View assigned duties.


2. Check Duty Chart – Know schedules in advance.


3. Receive Updates – Stay informed about any changes.



Simple, organized, and stress-free!


---

Slide 6: Key Benefits
✔ Admins: Faster, error-free duty allocation.
✔ Teachers: Easy access to schedules & updates.
✔ Institutions: Smooth, transparent exam management.


---

Slide 7: Live Demo (if applicable)
[Show a brief demonstration of the system’s key features.]


---

Slide 8: Conclusion
Our system eliminates errors, saves time, and improves efficiency in invigilation duty allocation.

Thank you! I’d be happy to answer any questions.


---

HIIIIII ABSKSHSKHKS Kar Mi give up kelay aaj sathi Udya karel  🙂‍↔️🙂‍↔️🙂‍↔️🙂‍↔️🙂‍↔️🙂‍↔️🙂‍↔️😭😭😭😭😭 Bc paging segmentation kaay aahe sagla null Here’s a detailed explanation of the different types of performing I/O operations in an Operating System:


---

1. Programmed I/O

Description:

CPU is actively involved in all I/O operations.

It sends a request to the I/O device and keeps checking (polling) if it’s ready.

Data transfer happens directly between the CPU and the I/O device.


How It Works:

CPU issues a command.

Waits (polls) until the device is ready.

Transfers data when ready.


Pros:

Simple to implement.

Useful for small, low-speed devices.


Cons:

Wastes CPU time (busy-waiting).

Inefficient for multitasking systems.



---

2. Interrupt-Driven I/O

Description:

CPU initiates the I/O operation and continues other work.

Device sends an interrupt to the CPU when it’s ready.

CPU then pauses, handles the interrupt using Interrupt Service Routine (ISR), and resumes.


How It Works:

CPU starts I/O → Device works in parallel → Sends interrupt when ready → CPU responds via ISR.


Pros:

Better CPU utilization than Programmed I/O.

Efficient for multi-tasking.


Cons:

Some overhead due to interrupt handling.

Complex logic for multiple interrupts.



---

3. Direct Memory Access (DMA)

Description:

A special hardware unit called DMA controller handles the data transfer directly between I/O device and memory without involving the CPU.

CPU is only involved at the start and end of the process.


How It Works:

CPU sets up the DMA: source, destination, size.

DMA controller handles data transfer.

Sends an interrupt when done.


Pros:

Very efficient for large data transfers (e.g., disk to memory).

Frees up CPU completely during transfer.


Cons:

More complex hardware.

Possible bus contention between CPU and DMA.



---

Comparison Table


---

4. Summary


---

Let me know if you want diagrams or revision flashcards on this! Here’s a detailed explanation of various Disk Scheduling Methods used in Operating Systems to manage how read/write requests are handled on a disk:


---

What is Disk Scheduling?

When multiple I/O requests are waiting for disk access, the Disk Scheduling Algorithm decides the order in which these requests should be processed to optimize performance like seek time, transfer rate, and throughput.


---

Key Terms to Know:

Seek Time: Time taken to move the disk arm to the required track.

Rotational Latency: Time waiting for the disk to rotate to the correct sector.

Throughput: Number of requests serviced per unit time.



---

1. FCFS (First Come First Serve)

How it works:

Requests are handled in the order they arrive.


Example:

If requests are: 98, 183, 37, 122
They are served in the same sequence.

Pros:

Simple and fair.


Cons:

Poor performance; high average seek time.

Doesn’t consider the current head position.



---

2. SSTF (Shortest Seek Time First)

How it works:

Services the request closest to the current head position.


Example:

If head is at 100, and requests are 95, 180, 34
Next will be 95 (shortest distance = 5).

Pros:

Better performance than FCFS.


Cons:

May cause starvation of distant requests.



---

3. SCAN (Elevator Algorithm)

How it works:

Disk arm moves in one direction servicing all requests, then reverses direction (like an elevator).


Example:

Head moves from track 0 to max and back, serving all requests in its path.

Pros:

Reduces variance in response time.


Cons:

Edge tracks are serviced less frequently.



---

4. LOOK

How it works:

Similar to SCAN but only goes as far as the last request in each direction, then reverses.


Example:

Doesn’t go to the end of the disk if no request is there.

Pros:

More efficient than SCAN.

Avoids unnecessary traversal.



---

5. C-SCAN (Circular SCAN)

How it works:

Like SCAN, but only moves in one direction.

When it reaches the end, it goes back to the beginning without servicing on the return trip.


Pros:

More uniform wait time.

Prevents requests on one end from being starved.



---

6. C-LOOK

How it works:

Same as LOOK, but circular.

Goes only as far as the last request in one direction, then jumps back to the start.


Pros:

Efficient with uniform service.



---

Comparison Table:


---

7. Choosing the Right Algorithm

SSTF for performance-critical systems but be cautious of starvation.

SCAN/LOOK for systems that need fairness.

C-SCAN/C-LOOK for high-throughput systems with uniform request distribution.



---

**Vedant (Marathi Speech):**
1. **Lack of attention:** Vedant faced a significant barrier due to the minimal attention given to his speech by the class. This lack of attention resulted in a lack of engagement and interaction, leading to reduced effectiveness in conveying his message.
2. **Language barrier:** Since Vedant delivered his speech in Marathi, students who were not proficient in Marathi faced difficulty in understanding his message. This language barrier hindered effective communication and limited the reach of his speech to only those who understood Marathi.
3. **Limited engagement:** The low level of interest and engagement from the class meant that Vedant's message did not resonate or connect with the majority of the audience. This limited engagement resulted in a less impactful delivery of his speech.
4. **Emotional expression:** Expressing emotions and nuances effectively in a less familiar language like Marathi can be challenging. Vedant may have faced difficulty in conveying the full range of emotions and subtleties in his message, impacting the overall effectiveness of his communication.
5. **Reduced impact:** Overall, the combination of low attention, language barriers, limited engagement, and challenges in emotional expression led to a reduced impact of Vedant's speech, as it did not leave a lasting impression or resonate strongly with the audience.

**Yukta (English Speech):**
1. **Potential distraction:** Yukta faced the potential barrier of distraction caused by the disruption during Nachiket's speech. This distraction could have affected her concentration and ability to deliver her message effectively.
2. **Language barrier:** Although Yukta delivered her speech in English, students who were not proficient in English may have struggled to fully understand her message. This language barrier could have hindered effective communication and comprehension.
3. **Pressure to deliver:** With the class instructed to pay full attention to her speech, Yukta may have felt pressure to deliver a clear, impactful, and engaging message. This pressure could have influenced her delivery style and communication approach.
4. **Adjustment in pace or style:** Yukta might have had to adjust her pace or style of delivery based on the varying levels of English proficiency among the audience. Adapting to different audience members' comprehension levels can be a challenging aspect of effective communication.
5. **Varied comprehension:** Due to the varied levels of English proficiency among the audience, Yukta's message may have been understood differently by different students. This variation in comprehension levels could have affected the overall impact and effectiveness of her communication.

**Nachiket (Hindi Speech):**
1. **Disturbance:** Nachiket faced a significant barrier due to the disturbance caused by the class's disruptive behavior, such as using mobile phones, playing music, and asking irrelevant questions. This disturbance disrupted the flow of his speech and hindered effective communication.
2. **Lack of attention:** As the class was instructed to pay no attention to Nachiket's speech, he faced a barrier in terms of lack of attention and respect from the audience. This lack of attention devalued his message and hindered effective communication.
3. **Inability to deliver effectively:** Constant interruptions and disturbances during Nachiket's speech made it challenging for him to deliver his message effectively. The disruptive environment limited his ability to express his thoughts clearly and coherently.
4. **Frustration and annoyance:** The disrespectful behavior of the audience, such as disturbing Nachiket's speech intentionally, may have led to feelings of frustration and annoyance on his part. These negative emotions can further hinder effective communication.
5. **Limited opportunity to showcase skills:** Due to the unfavorable environment created by the class's behavior and lack of attention, Nachiket had a limited opportunity to showcase his communication skills and express his thoughts effectively. Mi mazha example deto.
When I am frustrated= I start scribbling on a paper

When I'm sad abt any situation - I think of more worse thing that could have happened. That makes me feel ki what happened wasn't that bad

When I'm anxious abt anything, I start  playing chess or watch yt

When I'm panicking - I imagine what will a person that I respect the most will do in the same situation. For me it's 12th tution che Chemisty sir. I will try to think like them

Mega block aa udya Tham bghto ## CR - Central Railway to operate 63 hrs Special Block at Thane and 36 hrs Special Block at CSMT in connection with widening / extension of Platforms from mid-night of 30/31.5.2024 (Thursday/Friday night) to afternoon of 02.6.2024-Repurcussions on suburban services

THE DETAILS OF THE BLOCKS ARE AS UNDER:

A. BLOCK 1 – 63 hrs Special Block at Thane (DN Fast line)

Date & Duration of Block: From 00.30 hrs of 30/31.05.2024 (Thursday/Friday midnight) to 15:30 hrs of 02.06.2024 (Sunday afternoon) = 63 Hrs

Block Section:
UP Slow Line :Kalva (including CSMT end crossovers) to Thane (including all crossovers)
DN Fast Line :Thane (including all crossovers) to Kalva (including all crossovers)
UP Fast Line :Kalva (including all crossovers) to Thane (including all crossovers).

B. BLOCK 2 – 36 hrs Special Block at CSMT

Date of Block: From 00.30 hrs of 31.5.2024/01.6.2024 (Friday/Saturday midnight) to 12.30 hrs of 02.6.2024 (Sunday afternoon) - 36 hours

Duration of the block:
DN Fast Line : 00.30 hrs (Thursday/Friday night) to 15:30 hrs Sunday
UP Slow Line : 00.30 hrs (Thursday/Friday night) to 12:30 hrs Friday day

Block Section:
UP and DOWN Harbour lines between CSMT (including) and Vadala Road (excluding), UP and DOWN slow lines between CSMT (including) and Byculla (excluding),
UP and DOWN fast lines between CSMT (including) and Byculla (excluding)

REPERCUSSIONS ON SUBURBAN TRAINS DURING THE BLOCK
Cancellation of suburban services:

930 suburban services will be cancelled during the block period as follows:
161 services will be cancelled on 31.5.2024 (Friday)
534 services will be cancelled on 01.6.2024 (Saturday)
235 services will be cancelled on 02.6.2024 (Sunday)

Short termination of suburban services:
444 suburban services will be short terminated during the block period as follows:
7 services will be short terminated on 31.5.2024 (Friday)
306 services will be short terminated on 01.6.2024 (Saturday)
131 services will be short terminated on 02.6.2024 (Sunday)

Short origination of suburban services:
446 suburban services will short originate during the block period as follows:
307 services will short originate on 01.6.2024 (Saturday)
139 services will short originate on 02.6.2024 (Sunday)

Kaama pun kara sobat Ani coding pun Vach he Or maybe dono sath mein hehe Padh ye Error 404 Rukh GIVE ME A PYTHON PROGRAM TO RENAME EACH PNG FILE IN A GOOGLE DRIVE ACCORDING TO THE ROLL NO. AND NAME PROVIDED IN THE EXCEL FILE. THE FORMAT SHOULD BE :
format : ROLL NO. FULL NAME FROM EXCEL.png  (name in caps)
example :  1.BADHE CHAITANYA RAGHUNATH.png To accomplish the task of renaming PNG files in a Google Drive folder according to the roll number and name provided in an Excel file, you would need to perform the following steps:

1. **Read the Excel file** to extract roll numbers and names.
2. **Connect to Google Drive** using the Google Drive API.
3. **Rename each PNG file** according to the roll number and full name from the Excel file.

Since I cannot access Google Drive directly in this environment, I'll provide you with a Python script that you can run in your local environment.

### Step 1: Set up the Environment
1. **Install Required Libraries**:
```bash
pip install pandas google-auth google-auth-oauthlib google-auth-httplib2 google-api-python-client
```

2. **Set Up Google Drive API**:

### Step 2: Python Script

```python
import pandas as pd
import os
from google.oauth2 import service_account
from googleapiclient.discovery import build
from googleapiclient.http import MediaFileUpload

# Define the path to your Excel file and the Google Drive folder ID
excel_file_path = '/mnt/data/ATTENDANCE SHEET.xlsx'
drive_folder_id = '1x35CYKGhj0GG_76Mw7VIdTnz3-pSUuwd'

# Load the Excel file
df = pd.read_excel(excel_file_path)

# Define your credentials and build the Drive service
SERVICE_ACCOUNT_FILE = '/path/to/credentials.json'

credentials = service_account.Credentials.from_service_account_file(
SERVICE_ACCOUNT_FILE, scopes=SCOPES)
service = build('drive', 'v3', credentials=credentials)

# Function to rename files on Google Drive
def rename_files_on_drive(drive_service, folder_id, df):
# List all files in the specified Google Drive folder
query = f"'{folder_id}' in parents and mimeType='image/png'"
results = drive_service.files().list(q=query, fields="files(id, name)").execute()
files = results.get('files', [])

for file in files:
file_id = file['id']
file_name = file['name']

# Extract roll number and name from the DataFrame
roll_no, full_name = extract_roll_and_name(file_name, df)
if roll_no and full_name:
new_name = f"{roll_no}.{full_name}.png"

# Rename the file on Google Drive
file_metadata = {'name': new_name}
drive_service.files().update(fileId=file_id, body=file_metadata).execute()
print(f"Renamed file {file_name} to {new_name}")

def extract_roll_and_name(file_name, df):
# This function assumes that the file name matches with roll no or name in some way
for _, row in df.iterrows():
roll_no = str(row['ROLL NO']).strip()
full_name = row['FULL NAME'].upper().strip()
if roll_no in file_name or full_name.split()[0] in file_name:
return roll_no, full_name
return None, None

# Call the function to rename the files
rename_files_on_drive(service, drive_folder_id, df)
```

### Steps to Run the Script
1. **Ensure the `credentials.json` file** is in the correct path as specified in `SERVICE_ACCOUNT_FILE`.
2. **Run the script** in your local Python environment.

### Explanation:
- The script reads the roll number and full name from the Excel file.
- It then connects to Google Drive, lists all PNG files in the specified folder, and renames them according to the format provided.

Make sure to adjust the script as needed based on your specific file structure and requirements. If you're unable to use Python, you can use other languages to accomplish the task of renaming files in Google Drive according to the roll numbers and names provided in an Excel file. Here are a few alternatives:

### 1. **JavaScript (Node.js)**
- **Libraries**: You can use `googleapis` for interacting with Google Drive and `xlsx` for reading Excel files.
- **Advantages**: Node.js is widely used for backend tasks, and there are well-maintained libraries for Google APIs.

### Example Script:
```javascript
const {google} = require('googleapis');
const fs = require('fs');
const xlsx = require('xlsx');

// Load Excel file
const workbook = xlsx.readFile('/path/to/ATTENDANCE_SHEET.xlsx');
const sheet_name_list = workbook.SheetNames;
const df = xlsx.utils.sheet_to_json(workbook.Sheets[sheet_name_list[0]]);

// Google Drive API Setup
const auth = new google.auth.GoogleAuth({
keyFile: '/path/to/credentials.json',
scopes: SCOPES,
});
const drive = google.drive({version: 'v3', auth});

async function renameFilesOnDrive(folderId, df) {
const res = await drive.files.list({
q: `'${folderId}' in parents and mimeType='image/png'`,
fields: 'files(id, name)',
});

const files = res.data.files;
for (const file of files) {
const fileName = file.name;
const rollNoAndName = extractRollAndName(fileName, df);
if (rollNoAndName) {
const newName = `${rollNoAndName}.png`;
await drive.files.update({
fileId: file.id,
requestBody: {name: newName},
});
console.log(`Renamed ${fileName} to ${newName}`);
}
}
}

function extractRollAndName(fileName, df) {
for (const row of df) {
const rollNo = row['ROLL NO'].toString().trim();
const fullName = row['FULL NAME'].toUpperCase().trim();
if (fileName.includes(rollNo) || fileName.includes(fullName.split(' ')[0])) {
return `${rollNo}.${fullName}`;
}
}
return null;
}

renameFilesOnDrive('YOUR_FOLDER_ID', df);
```

### 2. **Java**
- **Libraries**: Use the `Google Drive API client library` for Java and `Apache POI` to read Excel files.
- **Advantages**: Java is a robust, statically typed language often used in enterprise environments.

### 3. **C#**
- **Libraries**: You can use `Google.Apis.Drive.v3` for Google Drive and `NPOI` or `EPPlus` for Excel file handling.
- **Advantages**: C# is powerful, especially in environments where Windows-based development is prevalent.

### 4. **PHP**
- **Libraries**: `google/apiclient` for Google Drive and `phpoffice/phpspreadsheet` for Excel file handling.
- **Advantages**: PHP is widely used for web applications and is easy to set up.

### 5. **Bash Script**
- **Tools**: You could use `curl` for API requests and `csvtool` or `awk` to process a CSV version of the Excel file.
- **Advantages**: Bash scripting is straightforward and can be useful for quick tasks on Unix-based systems.

### Example in Bash (Basic Concept):
```bash
#!/bin/bash

folder_id="YOUR_FOLDER_ID"
access_token="YOUR_ACCESS_TOKEN"

# Loop through PNG files in the directory
for file in *.png; do
# Extract roll number and name from CSV (converted from Excel)
roll_no=$(awk -F, '/filename/ {print $1}' data.csv)
name=$(awk -F, '/filename/ {print $2}')

# Format new name
new_name="${roll_no}.${name}.png"

# Rename file using Google Drive API
curl -X PATCH \
-H "Authorization: Bearer $access_token" \
-H "Content-Type: application/json" \
-d '{"name": "'$new_name'"}' \
done
```

### 6. **Ruby**
- **Libraries**: Use `google-api-client` for Drive API and `rubyXL` for reading Excel files.
- **Advantages**: Ruby is known for its simplicity and readability.

Each language has its advantages and is chosen based on your comfort level, the complexity of the task, and the environment you're working in. Let me know if you'd like a detailed example in one of these languages! Heheh Try karto hotay ka Yes yes

I do know a few things about Chess that I’d be happy to share.} 2. d4 cxd4 {Did
you know the second book ever printed in English was about Chess $2} 3. Qxd4 {All
my data is showing that you have an obvious move.} 3... e6 {There are now 5362
unique chess positions.} 4. Nf3 {Remember that your goal is to control the
center.} 4... h5 {I have calculated my options and this is the best one.} 5. Bc4
Nc6 {The knight has a value of about three pawns.} 6. Qe3 {You really seem like
you know what you’re doing. Who programmed you $2} 6... Qc7 {Based on the outcome
of 6931 simulated games, I believe this is the optimal move.} 7. Nc3 b5 {I just
wanted to give you a warning that I’m targeting your piece.} 8. Bxb5 {Are you
sure you’re not a bot as well $2} 8... f6 {Wumpus was originally created to greet
new people on Discord because Wumpus had no friends :(} 9. O-O {I’ve studied a
lot of games and that was a great move.} 9... Nge7 {I’d be happy to explain why
I made this move after the game.} 10. Nd4 Nxd4 {I just want to say that if I
could feel fun I’d be having it.} 11. Qxd4 {Hmm it seems I made that too
obvious…} 11... Ng6 {Hopefully you can forgive me for putting you in a tough
spot.} 12. Re1 Qe5 {Somethings not right, a glitch perhaps $2} 13. Qxe5 {You just
took my queen. Wha… ~brrrzzzzz~ WHO PROGRAMMED ME $2} 13... Nxe5 {You didn’t make
that too obvious. I’m just a bot that can see many moves ahead. Like billions.}
14. Bf4 Rb8 {The rook’s name comes from the Persian word “rukh” meaning
chariot.} 15. Bxe5 {I value the bishop slightly higher than the knight.} 15...
fxe5 {After running the numbers, it seems there’s an obvious move for me to
make.} 16. b3 {Do you ever feel like you’re just a pawn in some big game $2 No $2
Yeah… Me neither.} 16... Bc5 {Did you know the bishop and knight are worth the
same amount of points $2} 17. Bc4 Bb4 {Did you know Discord started as a game
company making a mobile game called Fates Forever $2} 18. Re3 Bxc3 {After double
checking my data, a trade would be best in this scenario.} 19. Rxc3 {I see this
is going to be more difficult than I had planned.} 19... h4 20. h3 Rh6 21. Rd1
{The rook is worth the second most behind the queen.} 21... g6 22. a4 Rb6 23.
Bb5 {“I feel a threat to my piece” is what I would say if I was capable of
feelings.} 23... Rxb5 {I’ve learned humans like to apologize in these
scenarios.} 24. Rxc8+ {It seems I’ve left my king vulnerable. But… Why would I
do that $2 Bzzt. Brrp. Beep.} 24... Ke7 {You can play Discord’s version of the
Snake game on our 404 page by pressing a “secret” button.} 25. axb5 {That is

No problem with canva but I think to design the magazine in a more professional manner, I would recommend adobe indesign because with it, there are plenty of templates available which will reduce our workload to some extent, and we can focus more on the formatting Whereas in canva, we would need a separate team for creating a template and another team for scrutinising data and adding (along with formatting) Well indesign also has its downsides. It needs a little beefy computer and it’s paid, so if you work on mac then it’s next to impossible to include that in our workflow Aree ek help pahije hoti Tula mahiti na apan dupari kai discuss kela te

(PPT) Noicee Bhai te report pathav na Phy cha Kay hota te Khagesh chya grp ne banvalela ig Tycha navtha te But yea tyacha pan same aahe topic Pathavto Koncha Chnaglay aahe tyacha pathva Missed voice call Lesgoo This message was deleted Broooo where tf is this streamingggggg Good morning everyone, myself Nachiket Patil along with my acquaintance (name) are here to present our physics project.

The topic of our project is Spectrometry and DIY spectrometer.

Here are the points we will cover in this presentation.

Firstly, our objective to choose this topic is "To provide a comprehensive understanding of Spectrometry, it's principles and real world application and to empower the audience with the knowledge and skills to build a DIY spectrometer for practical experiment"

So, without further delay let's get started with what exactly is Spectrometry. "Spectrometry is the measurement of the interactions between light and matter, and the reactions and measurements of radiation intensity and wavelength. In other words, spectrometry is a method of studying and measuring a specific spectrum, and it's widely used for the spectroscopic analysis of sample materials. The instrument used for measuring is known as a spectrometer."
"Spectrometry is based on the principle that when matter interacts with electromagnetic radiation such as light of x rays it can absorb, emit or scatter radiation at specific wavelengths. By measuring these interactions, scientists can gain valueable information about the substance being analysed."

Few types of spectrometry are (types) . These types vary from their application in a particular field of research

We will focus on optical spectrometry.
"Optical Spectrometry is a technique that measures the spectrum of light emitted, absorbed or scattered by a substance. This technique is commonly used to study the properties of celestial objects". "Ever wondered how scientists discovered which elements are present in Cosmic Clouds ?
They did it with the help of Spectrometry"

Let's learn it in depth.
We know Visible light is a part of the electromagnetic spectrum, and white light is a combination of all visible lights, ie. from wavelength 400nm to 700 nm.
Naturally when white light from the sun passes through a prism it gets diffracted into its corresponding colours, thus forming a continuous spectrum.

When gasses like Hydrogen,oxygen, nitrogen are enclosed in a tube and current is passed through them, they start to emit light of different wavelengths. Which can be measured by a spectrometer

While, this happens because when the current is passed it makes the electron jump from higher energy orbit to lower energy orbit. Which leads to the release of energy in the form of photons and this creates an emission spectrum. For example this is the emission spectrum of hydrogen. Helium, sodium and magnesium

Now when we look at celestial bodies through telescopes allowing only these particular wavelengths, we can calculate how much of that element is present there. For example this is the amount of hydrogen present on the surface of the sun and this is the amount of oxygen. In the similar way scientists found  the elements of cosmic clouds

Coming back to the topic, as we saw earlier, wavelengths of lights in the emission spectrum are calculated with the help of a Spectrometer. This is how a conventional spectrometer looks like. We calculate the angles at which we see the colours, then from the formula (a+b) sin theta / n = lambda we get the wavelength. Now, this is our DIY spectrometer

(name) will explain the working of this spectrometer.

There is a thin slit at the very front of the box which allows very little light to enter.

This light is then diffracted by diffraction grading. Diffraction grading is just a thin slit which contains small prisms. In our case we will use a CD drive, which works perfectly fine.

This diffracted light is then captured by a  webcam. Which is connected to a program called "Theremino" which gives us the exact spectrum of entering light along with its wavelength.

These are a few expected observations.
1. Spectrum of white led, we can see how white led is a combination of Red, Blue and Green light.
2. Spectrum of purple led, from this we can infer that there is no such colour as purple, it's just a combination of Blue and Red which fools our eyes in thinking as a single colour.
3. And this is the spectrum of Infrared signals from a TV remote

The conclusion of this presentation is
That we learnt about spectrometry, its applications and how a diy spectrometer works.

Finally these are some references that we used while researching on this topic.

Today I'm going to talk about Social Media. Do you guys know that the first Social networking site was launched in 1997 by the name of Six Degrees. Since then, social media has ingrained itself into our daily lives to the point where the average person uses it for two and a half hours every day. I have no doubt that the first thing we will do after leaving this room is check Instagram. Check if there is a new like or comment on ur post, check if there is a new trend, new message or whether your crush has finally responded to you. Social media has its pros and cons so Fasten your seatbelts, my friends, as we dive in this digital dilemma. Are we becoming slaves to the screen, or are we crafting a new era of communication and connectivity? Whether social media is a boon or a bane.

Social media is an enormous platform to showcase your skills, to advertise your products, to freely express your opinion on any topic, to gain influence and many more. With the rise of social media, there is a rise in career opportunities. For example, social media influencers, editors, digital marketers, PR teams etc. Think about the influencers we encounter, like Ankit Bayapuriya, who turned a self-improvement challenge into a movement. Or the channels like Abhi and Niyu who keep us updated with current affairs. But not all influencers are cut from the same cloth. Ever heard of the 10-day MBA guru ? It's like a shortcut to success, but is it genuine or a marketing maze? The choices we make navigating these digital pathways define not only our perceptions but our very digital personas. So Be selective with who you invest your time, because wasted time is worse than wasted money.

This brings me to the second point I want to talk about. Time. Does anyone know how these social media giants earn when their apps are free to download and use ? How do they pay their bills ? Or how do they pay their employees ? You might have heard this "If the product is free then you consumers are the product", yes they earn by selling our time. The more time you spend scrolling through those endless feeds, the more data these social media giants collect. They know what posts you like, the places you visit, the words you search for – it's all in the data. And guess what? They use this  Data to bombard you with ads tailored to your needs. Advertising companies pay big bucks, millions in fact, to these platforms for the privilege of targeting you. Recent studies by Cambridge Analytica show that the average attention span of teenagers has decreased by 18%, which means a user would rather be interested in watching a 1 min reel rather than a 5 min long video. Companies like Instagram and Facebook have hence made reels or short form content as their main weapon to keep users engaged. But let's be honest, some of the stuff on those reels is downright cringe-worthy. Can we all agree on that ? I'm so grateful to the Indian Government for banning TikTok.

Coming back to the topic. We are students of Data Science and we know the importance of data. When we login into a social media platform We don't know what data of ours is being collected we don't know how and where our data is being used. We don't know if the posts we share are in safe hands. Also There are thousands of data breaches happening every single day. Because of this Piracy, online bullying and hacking are some of the issues we should really be concerned about. And voila with the power of AI you get to hear incidents like that of Deepfake video of the famous Actress Rashmika Mandana. Let me recall it for those who don't know. So basically some anonymous guy collected all the images and videos of Rashmika and fed it into an AI along with a disturbing video of some other lady. And this AI swapped that lady's face with seamlessly merging Rashmika's face, expressions, and even her actual voice. And thus as the name suggests created a Deepfake video. Such a shameful act. Luckily the person who did this is caught and is behind the bars now but this gets me thinking. What if overnight someone makes a Deepfake video of our PM Narendra Modi saying "Hey America, we were behind the terrorist attack of 9/11" And the next day you wake up with the Roaring sounds of America fighter jets ready to drop a bomb. Okay i know  that was too much of an exaggeration but The point I want to highlight is that the news or controversies we hear on social media are not always true or are sometimes biased towards one party.  We cannot trust the anonymous user sitting on the other side of the screen with his intentions. We are unsure if the message he is conveying is true or just an attempt to deviate us from reality.

This brings me to my concluding point and I couldn't find any better way to explain it but in the words of my favourite standup comedian Vir Das. It goes like this. There will be a war very soon. And the next war is not going to be good versus evil, it's not even going to be truth versus truth. It will be reality versus reality. It will be truth versus truth. Your truth versus their truth. We won't even need to build weapons anymore. Remember how throughout world wars billionaires would start pivoting their industries towards making weapons ? Why don't they do that anymore ? Why is every single billionaire trying to buy a social media platform. It's because you are the weapon. Your attention is the ammunition. **Vedant (Marathi Speech):**
1. **Lack of attention:** Vedant faced a significant barrier due to the minimal attention given to his speech by the class. This lack of attention resulted in a lack of engagement and interaction, leading to reduced effectiveness in conveying his message.
2. **Language barrier:** Since Vedant delivered his speech in Marathi, students who were not proficient in Marathi faced difficulty in understanding his message. This language barrier hindered effective communication and limited the reach of his speech to only those who understood Marathi.
3. **Limited engagement:** The low level of interest and engagement from the class meant that Vedant's message did not resonate or connect with the majority of the audience. This limited engagement resulted in a less impactful delivery of his speech.
4. **Emotional expression:** Expressing emotions and nuances effectively in a less familiar language like Marathi can be challenging. Vedant may have faced difficulty in conveying the full range of emotions and subtleties in his message, impacting the overall effectiveness of his communication.
5. **Reduced impact:** Overall, the combination of low attention, language barriers, limited engagement, and challenges in emotional expression led to a reduced impact of Vedant's speech, as it did not leave a lasting impression or resonate strongly with the audience.

**Yukta (English Speech):**
1. **Potential distraction:** Yukta faced the potential barrier of distraction caused by the disruption during Nachiket's speech. This distraction could have affected her concentration and ability to deliver her message effectively.
2. **Language barrier:** Although Yukta delivered her speech in English, students who were not proficient in English may have struggled to fully understand her message. This language barrier could have hindered effective communication and comprehension.
3. **Pressure to deliver:** With the class instructed to pay full attention to her speech, Yukta may have felt pressure to deliver a clear, impactful, and engaging message. This pressure could have influenced her delivery style and communication approach.
4. **Adjustment in pace or style:** Yukta might have had to adjust her pace or style of delivery based on the varying levels of English proficiency among the audience. Adapting to different audience members' comprehension levels can be a challenging aspect of effective communication.
5. **Varied comprehension:** Due to the varied levels of English proficiency among the audience, Yukta's message may have been understood differently by different students. This variation in comprehension levels could have affected the overall impact and effectiveness of her communication.

**Nachiket (Hindi Speech):**
1. **Disturbance:** Nachiket faced a significant barrier due to the disturbance caused by the class's disruptive behavior, such as using mobile phones, playing music, and asking irrelevant questions. This disturbance disrupted the flow of his speech and hindered effective communication.
2. **Lack of attention:** As the class was instructed to pay no attention to Nachiket's speech, he faced a barrier in terms of lack of attention and respect from the audience. This lack of attention devalued his message and hindered effective communication.
3. **Inability to deliver effectively:** Constant interruptions and disturbances during Nachiket's speech made it challenging for him to deliver his message effectively. The disruptive environment limited his ability to express his thoughts clearly and coherently.
4. **Frustration and annoyance:** The disrespectful behavior of the audience, such as disturbing Nachiket's speech intentionally, may have led to feelings of frustration and annoyance on his part. These negative emotions can further hinder effective communication.
5. **Limited opportunity to showcase skills:** Due to the unfavorable environment created by the class's behavior and lack of attention, Nachiket had a limited opportunity to showcase his communication skills and express his thoughts effectively. Now gets(a) reads the lines of text and stores it in string

Wait so gets(a) meko bhi confuse Kiya so here I'm sharing what I found online. Read it then we will proceed wait ait i had searched it up dekha maine The `gets(a)` function reads a line of text from the standard input (usually the keyboard) and stores it as a string in the character array `a`.

1. **Reading Input:**
- The `gets(a)` function reads characters from the standard input stream until it encounters a newline (`\n`) character or the end-of-file (EOF) marker.
- It stores the characters in the array `a` and terminates the string with a null character (`\0`) to mark the end of the string.

2. **Character Array Size:**
- It's important to note that `gets(a)` does not perform bounds checking on the array `a`, meaning it will read characters into `a` without checking if there is enough space.
- This lack of bounds checking makes `gets` unsafe to use because it can lead to buffer overflow vulnerabilities if the input string is longer than the size of the array `a`.

3. **Unsafe Function:**
- Due to its lack of bounds checking, the `gets` function is considered unsafe and deprecated in modern C programming.
- It's recommended to use safer alternatives such as `fgets` for reading input into character arrays to avoid buffer overflow issues. bye Uhh nhi ho hi Okay so after that we get the number of elements by using a while loop to check whether any element of a[] is null pointer (\0 is known as null pointer) Are you aware of what is null pointer Uhh Ig you should take some rest for now Or is there anything that is bothering you ? mhanje haina aikna tu pudhche explain karun thev na llile text I'll see subah ismorry 🥹 Na chodh phir areeey I won't like if it's not one-to-one i wanna know Kaal subh samjavto Jhop ata pakka? aaa sorry oye oyeeeee nachi ket heloM ? History - So while coding the frontend of a website suppose u have to check how well the text paragraph fits in a place, let's say you add an image at left and you want to see how well the text will align in the place at the right, so you wrote Lorem times (some number of words) in the code editor.
Eg - loremX100
And this will fill that empty space with 100 random words.
You can say it's a programmer's slang to just fill in something and think about the name later.

Just like this flower is unique, you are unique. All of us have something special that makes us as beautiful. Do you know what makes you special?
Now the answer to that can be a little difficult to find, because sometimes life has a cruel way of picking out your petals, breaking you in two and throwing you into the trash. Now when you’re broken, it’s very difficult to feel special.

Mr Contest Chair, my fellow flowers. I can remember the first time I broke. I was 17 years old. I had already flunked high school and managed to get myself arrested. Now, I wasn’t afraid of the cops, but there was one person I was very afraid of and that was my mama. Raise your hand if you have an emotional mother. Let me see. Put them all together you get my mama. I can hear her scream outside the police station; even the cops were afraid. She came up to me, held the iron bars, looked into my eyes and I saw a tear coming down her face.

Now I’ve seen my mama cry before, but mothers cry three types of tears: tears of joy, tears of sorrow and tears of shame. And when a son sees a mother cry tears of shame, that’s a life-changing moment. She looked at me and said, “Son, I want you to be a better man”. That night, when I drove home, my dad was waiting for me at home.

Now, my dad is a cool dad. Raise your hand if you have a cool dad. Put them all together you get my dad. My dad came up to me and said “Son, it’s OK. You flunked your exams. You already got arrested. That’s fine. You get that from your mother's side. I want you to start working immediately”. And I said, ‘OK.’

So my dad took me to meet one of his friends called Sam. Now, Sam was an accountant who had an accounting firm and had generously decided to make me his personal assistant, and there he was. He looked like a teddy bear, but this man was special. I looked at him and he looked at me, and then he said the most amazing thing. He said “Son, I see something in you, but I don’t know what it is. If you decide to work with me, I can help you find that something”. And I was like, wow!, that’s the first time in my whole life somebody has ever told they see something in me. And I started working for Sam.

And every day after work he used to tell me stories about the world, about history, about culture, about philosophy and it was much more interesting than what I learned in school. And I discovered I can dream and I started dreaming, ladies and gentlemen. After one year I went back into high school, completed my exams and went into college.

After successfully completing college, I found a great girl, but not a job. I didn’t know what I wanted to do with my life. Have you ever had that problem? And when you’re lost, it’s difficult to feel special. So I went back to my cool dad and I said: “Dad, I feel lost”.

He said, “You are like your mother.”

So my dad introduced me to this strange club that had a strange name, with strange people, talking.
On the first meeting, they told me to do something called a table topic. I aced it. But while I was speaking I see a strange man seated in the back row, humble, simple, the unfailing quality of kindness in his eyes. As soon as I finished, he walked up to me, looked me dead straight in the eye and said, “Son, I see something in you, but I don’t know what it is. If you come here twice a month maybe we can find that something.”

And ladies and gentlemen, I discovered I could speak and I love speaking and that led me to become a teacher. I know what it’s like to not have enough money in your bank account. I know what it’s like to worry when the bills start coming in. And sometimes in the middle of the night, I wake up my beautiful wife and ask her “Honey, why did you marry me?”

She says, “I saw something in you, but I still I don’t know what it is”

Ladies and gentlemen, today I’m a dreamer, I’m a speaker and I learned the unfailing quality of unconditional love from my wife.

I was broken and I’ve been broken, lost and broke many times in my life, but the people in my life were able to reach into the trash can and make me whole again. If it was up to me, I would have never been able to do that. And this is why if you have great people in your life, no matter how broke, how lost or how broken you become they can piece you back together.
Ladies and gentlemen, when I look at you I see something in you, but I don’t know what it is.
Over to you. Below is an outline of what should be stored in your database:

1. Users Table
User ID (Primary Key)
Name
Email
Phone Number
Password (hashed)
User Role (adviser or client)
Profile Picture URL
Account Status (active, suspended, etc.)
Registration Date
2. Advisers Table
Adviser ID (Primary Key)
Full Name
Email
Phone Number
Password (hashed)
Expertise Area (e.g., stock market, real estate)
Profile Picture URL
Bio/Description
Experience (years of experience)
Ratings (aggregate score)
Status (active, pending verification, suspended)
Verification Documents (URLs of uploaded documents)
Availability (days/hours for sessions)
Registration Date
3. Sessions Table
Session ID (Primary Key)
User ID (Foreign Key to Users Table)
Adviser ID (Foreign Key to Advisers Table)
Session Type (chat, video call, voice call)
Start Time
End Time
Session Status (scheduled, completed, canceled)
Notes (any notes shared between adviser and user)
Session Transcript (if you are storing text chats)
Session Rating (user-provided rating after the session)
4. Messages Table (if using real-time chat)
Message ID (Primary Key)
Session ID (Foreign Key to Sessions Table)
Sender ID (Foreign Key to Users or Advisers Table)
Message Content
Timestamp
5. Payments Table
Payment ID (Primary Key)
User ID (Foreign Key to Users Table)
Adviser ID (Foreign Key to Advisers Table)
Session ID (Foreign Key to Sessions Table)
Amount
Payment Method (credit card, PayPal, etc.)
Transaction Status (pending, completed, failed)
Payment Date
6. Reviews Table
Review ID (Primary Key)
User ID (Foreign Key to Users Table)
Adviser ID (Foreign Key to Advisers Table)
Session ID (Foreign Key to Sessions Table)
Rating (1-5 stars)
Review Text
Timestamp
7. Subscription Plans (optional)
Plan ID (Primary Key)
Plan Name (e.g., monthly, yearly)
Price
Features (number of sessions, adviser types available)
Duration (e.g., 1 month, 1 year)
Status (active, discontinued)
8. Notifications Table
Notification ID (Primary Key)
User ID (Foreign Key to Users Table)
Notification Type (e.g., session reminder, payment confirmation)
Message
Timestamp
Status (read, unread)
9. Admin Table
Admin ID (Primary Key)
Name
Email
Role (super admin, moderator)
Password (hashed)
Last Login
Why You Need a Database
A database is essential to:

Store all user, adviser, and session information persistently.
Track the progress and history of each session.
Record payments securely.
Manage authentication and user roles.
Provide scalability as more users join the platform.
You could use relational databases like MySQL or PostgreSQL for structured data, or even a NoSQL database like MongoDB if you want more flexibility in storing session logs and messages.

Let me know if you need help with database schema design or if you'd like more technical details on any of these tables! Try to implement the first 3 ohkay also THANK YOU SO MUCH YOU ARE ONE WHO ALWAYS HELPS ME THANKS 🥹❤️ You are welcome :) Hi
